  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_4505b7e1-1618-4175-91a9-5965be1fe4f8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer14408692570591638842">Jake Sullivan is a licensed Private Eye—with a seriously hardboiled attitude. He also possesses raw magical talent and the ability to make objects in his vicinity light as a feather or as heavy as depleted uranium, all with a magical thought.   <span id="freeText14408692570591638842" style="display:none">Jake Sullivan is a licensed Private Eye—with a seriously hardboiled attitude. He also possesses raw magical talent and the ability to make objects in his vicinity light as a feather or as heavy as depleted uranium, all with a magical thought. It's no wonder the G-men turn to Jake when they need someone to go after a suspected killer who's been knocking off banks in a magic-enhanced crime spree. Problems arise when Jake discovers the bad girl behind the robberies is an old friend, and he happens to know her magic is just as powerful as his, and the Feds have plunged Jake into a secret battle between powerful cartels of magic-users--a cartel whose ruthless leaders have decided that Jake is far too dangerous to live. . . .</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_166129626" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/166129626" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/166129626?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Correia fans and people who don't want to know about authors' politics</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to carol.  by: </span>
      Fantasy Aficionados
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=male-lead">male-lead</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=time-period-fantasy">time-period-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=steampunk">steampunk</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer166129626" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8160011182499364357">Unfortunately, Hard Magic doesn't measure up to Correia's first series, Monster Hunters International. One reviewer hit it on the head when he noted that there is a lack of world building, and tossed-in 1920s vocabulary is supposed to stand for setting. There's more detail on guns then there are physical characteristics of setting and mood, critical elements of the detective noir. There's a lot of odd ethnic referrals going on as well that make me vaguely uncomfortable. I don't know a lot about </span>
  <span id="freeText8160011182499364357" style="display:none">Unfortunately, Hard Magic doesn't measure up to Correia's first series, Monster Hunters International. One reviewer hit it on the head when he noted that there is a lack of world building, and tossed-in 1920s vocabulary is supposed to stand for setting. There's more detail on guns then there are physical characteristics of setting and mood, critical elements of the detective noir. There's a lot of odd ethnic referrals going on as well that make me vaguely uncomfortable. I don't know a lot about the 20s, but it almost seems if Correia is pulling on American political attitudes from the 40s-50s(post WWII) in his characterizations of Germans and Japanese and the political divisions. I get the feeling he didn't research the 1920s for this book--more like he watched a couple of Al Capone movies.<br /><br />I enjoyed Faye, the grey-eyed talented Okie kid who grows into her power, but I think I loved her because I root for grrl-power, and not because the characterization was done particularly well. Her simplistic speech pattern when we are inside her head need finesse as she progresses through her development. As usual, females play the "almost-but-not-quite-equal" role, despite the actions of Faye. One's a healer and one's a ex-prostitute (I believe there's an ex-ho in Monster as well), so you can pretty much tell from there how their characterization is going to run. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Yes, I get that Faye saved the day. However, she does so with a sense of glee and with her uneducated speech/text, and she's still technically a juvenile, so she's not equal or sophisticated enough to rank with the male leaders. Her end scene with the jellyfish might negate my assessment, but that section is a little to weird to analyze).  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />You can tell Correia put a lot of thought into the development of his Heavy, Sullivan. I liked the premise of the story, the fascinating idea of "powers" branching out into "adjacent" areas with practice.<br /><br />He is also taking the narrative short-cut of the almost-omniscient narrator, and flipping between a number of protagonists and antagonists. Despite the shift in narrators, there is one character "surprise" and a mediocre plot twist based on character premeditated plans in the last few pages of the book. It's a technique that irks me to no end for two reasons: one, because it feels like it's substituting character sketches for a congruent storyline; and two, it smacks of poor characterization--shouldn't we already be aware of their goals if we are in the characters' minds? <br /><br />Alright, so it's not the most positive of reviews, but you can see so many 5 and 4 star reviews, I don't really need to re-iterate what's good, do I? <br /><br /><br />** Stars removed 05/14 due to author behavior, generally being a lackwit and Hugo shenanigans. His latest blog is ranting against the campaign to raise awareness about the abducted schoolgirls, as well as mocking the men involved in the anti-pedophile campaign. Plus there's the whole effort to destroy the Hugos by "getting underrepresented white minority conservative writers" 'represented.' <a href="http://www.donotlink.com/hXj" rel="nofollow noopener">monsterhunternation.com</a><br /><br /><br /><br />If you are an anonymous poster who joined goodreads this month (whatever month that may be), have no personal details, or no reviews on this site, you can take your opinions and put them in an appropriate place--your own review. In other words, move along. I will delete your nonsense.<br /><br />BTW,<br />I also down-rated all his other books I read. For your trolling convenience:<br />#1: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show</a>...<br />#2: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/166129606">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br />#3: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show</a>...<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8160011182499364357" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_166261180" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/166261180" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/166261180?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=hardboiled-and-noir">hardboiled-and-noir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=signed-first-or-limited-edition">signed-first-or-limited-edition</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=sff-operation-chaotica">sff-operation-chaotica</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=good-guys">good-guys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer166261180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14310608871995198979"><b>WINNER:</b>...<b>BESTest</b>, most <b>FUN-Drenched</b> and <b>PAGE-Turniest</b> new hard-boiled, magical, steampunk, noirish, alternate history, gun-toting, action-orientated urban fantasy.<br/><br/>Larry Correia’s <i>Monster Hunter International</i> series has been guilty pleasure of mine for a few years. Now, with <i>Hard Magic</i>, the first of a new series called the Grimnoir Chronicles, Correia unloads the guilt and pumps up the pleasure by crafting a smart, authentic, incredibly fun alternate history in which magic has been incorporated </span>
  <span id="freeText14310608871995198979" style="display:none"><b>WINNER:</b>...<b>BESTest</b>, most <b>FUN-Drenched</b> and <b>PAGE-Turniest</b> new hard-boiled, magical, steampunk, noirish, alternate history, gun-toting, action-orientated urban fantasy.<br /><br />Larry Correia’s <i>Monster Hunter International</i> series has been guilty pleasure of mine for a few years. Now, with <i>Hard Magic</i>, the first of a new series called the Grimnoir Chronicles, Correia unloads the guilt and pumps up the pleasure by crafting a smart, authentic, incredibly fun alternate history in which magic has been incorporated into an otherwise recognizable world of the 1930’s. Correia’s growth as a writer and a story-teller has really been impressive and this is simply gold from the standpoint of page-turning entertainment and characters with whom you can really engage. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>BACKGROUND</u>
</b><br /><br />The world of <i>Hard Magic</i> began to diverge from our history in the 1850’s when individuals with magical powers (known as “Actives”) began appearing around the world. Actives are a small (but growing) percentage of the population and are generally viewed with suspicion and hate by the general population. For fans of the X-men, it’s akin to the persecution of mutants in the Marvel universe. <br /><br />Correia deftly incorporates the divergent history into the narrative including beginning each chapter with famous historical quotes that have been altered to include references to the presence of magic as a proven phenomenon. For example: <blockquote>
  <i>One general law, leading to the advancement of all organic beings, namely, multiply, vary, let the strongest live and the weakest die. The appearance of esoteric and ethereal abilities, magical fires and feats of strength, in recent decades are the purest demonstration of natural selection. Surely, in time, that general law will require the extinction of traditional man.<br /><br />--<u>Charles Darwin</u>, <b>On the Origin of Man and Selection of Human Magical Abilities</b>, (1879).</i>
</blockquote> These snippets are slick and a lot of fun and include things like Babe Ruth talking about hitting his 200th home run in a season and an altered version of Al Capone’s famous “kind word and a gun” line). In addition to being a real hoot, these commentaries help give Correia's world a genuine feeling of depth. <br /> <br />The magic system of <i>Hard Magic</i> really felt more like “super powers” than the stuff of sorcery and this made it both familiar and fresh at the same time. Each Active has access to a single magic/power and the varieties are amazing. Examples include teleportation, healing, pyrokinetics, electricity, invulnerability, super strength, telekinesis, density manipulation, super speed, ESP, etc... <br /><br />An interesting aspect to the magic is that each “actives” has a different “store” of energy that is used up when they perform their ability and then must be recharged. Thus, it is very possible to wear down an active and make them vulnerable to conventional attack. This provides a great avenue for tactics and strategy to play a part in the encounters between Actives and adds another layer of authenticity (relatively speaking) to the narrative. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>PLOT SUMMARY</u>
</b><br /><br />Jake Sullivan (no relation) is a war-hero, ex-con and a very powerful <b>Heavy</b> which means he has the ability to alter gravitational forces for both himself and those around him. When we first meet Jake, he is in prison for murdering a local sheriff who was abusing a fellow “Active.” Plain spoken, no nonsense Jake describes it this way:<blockquote>
  <i>The learned gentlemen from the university have asked me if I relied on Einstein’s General Theory of Relativity or if I used the simpler rules of Newton’s Law of Universal Gravitation on the evening in question when I accidentally took Sheriff Johnson’s life . Shit. I don’t know. I just got angry and squished the fucker. But I’ve gotten better at running things and I promise not to do it no more.<br /><br />--<u>Jake Sullivan</u>, <b>Parole Hearing, Rockville State Penitentiary</b> (1928)</i>
</blockquote> Jake is granted early parole by J. Edgar Hoover in exchange for working with the government to bring down dangerous “Actives” wanted for murder. While on a mission to bring down a dangerous “Brute” (i.e., super strength), Jake discovers that the Active in question is his old sweetheart Delilah. The confrontation leads Jake to the discovery that the government has been lying to him and he finds himself recruited by a magical society (the “Grimnoir”) that is involved in secret war against the evil Imperium (and alternate Japanese Empire run by the most powerful Active in the world, the Chairman). <br /><br />Larry Correia has created a fun, blockbuster of a world that have incorporated the use of magic in very interesting ways. You’ve got the German army using zombie soldiers thanks to the Kaiser’s powers of necromancy and the Imperium’s Iron Guard are a superb foe for the story. You have Actives known as “cogs” whose power is creative genius and so the world of the 1930’s has some surprises for the readers to discover. <br /><br />This is non-stop action from start to finish but is also loaded with fun concepts, endearing characters, a great sprinkling of clever alternative history, and a plot that is very interesting. There is so much to like in this story that I feel a significant man-crush forming for Mr. Correia who is now 3 for 3 in entertaining me with his work. This is easily the best of the three and shows that the author is only getting better as time goes on. I can’t wait to gobble up book 2 of the series when it comes out. <br /><br />5.0 stars. HIGHEST POSSIBLE RECOMMENDATION!!<br /><br />P.S. Bronson Pinchot does the narration of the audio version of this book and he is amazing…as usual. He definitely adds to the overall enjoyment of the work, especially with his accent for Jake Sullivan and the unusual cadence of the Pale Horse (an Active who can kill with a touch).<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14310608871995198979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1247469252" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1247469252" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1247469252?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1247469252" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17509676636533875927">When I started to read this book my expectations were completely different from what the book was about. Look at the cover; read the blurb; heck - read the title of the series. I expected something like Raymond Chandler or James M. Cain with some magic thrown in: an urban fantasy in the beginning of twentieth century. Instead I got X-Men set in twenties and general atmosphere of forties of the same century. <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1542505410i/26613560.jpg' alt='X-Men' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>To make my life easier I explain some plot elements it terms of X-Men world - I will put </span>
  <span id="freeText17509676636533875927" style="display:none">When I started to read this book my expectations were completely different from what the book was about. Look at the cover; read the blurb; heck - read the title of the series. I expected something like Raymond Chandler or James M. Cain with some magic thrown in: an urban fantasy in the beginning of twentieth century. Instead I got X-Men set in twenties and general atmosphere of forties of the same century. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1542505410i/26613560.jpg" alt="X-Men" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>To make my life easier I explain some plot elements it terms of X-Men world - I will put these explanations in parenthesis. Some time before the book events start some people (mutants) suddenly acquire supernatural abilities. A groups of such people with powerful abilities decided to create a secret society called Grimnoir (X-Men) to protect others with such abilities from normal people who naturally distrusted them and help the normal people. The biggest US branch of Grimnoir was led by General Black Jack Pershing (Professor Charles Francis Xavier). <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1542505629i/26613563.png" alt="Professor X" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>A new guy called Jake Sullivan (Wolverine) ended up in this Grimnoir cell practically against his will. <br><br>I can trace the further parallels, but will risk the wrath people to whom I give too many spoilers. So full stop with the plot. I liked the main character Jake Sullivan: he was well-developed and relatable. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1542505629i/26613564._SX540_.jpg" alt="Wolverine" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>A young girl Faye Vierra (Rogue) was at least interesting, but she definitely divided the opinion of reviewers. Some thought she was great, while others thought she was not strong enough, or too stereotypical, or not serious enough. In any way she made an impression. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1542505754i/26613566.jpg" alt="Rogue" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The action was great as I came to expect from Larry Correia. Now the question comes: why only 3 stars? For starters I already mentioned different expectations. I still think that what I expected would be better. Everybody who read Monster Hunter series already guessed the author is a big gun enthusiast and I expected some interesting gunfight scenes. However magic was deciding factor in any fight and guns ended up being meaningless; again despite what the cover suggests. <br><br>My second big problem with the book: there were too many points of view for my liking and switches between them happened way too often. Such frequent switches might work in epic fantasy - although I really hated them in Malazan Book of Fallen - but in any other subgenre of fantasy it only serves to annoy.<br><br>Too many good people bit the dust while baddies just shrugged and kept doing their nefarious deeds. It would not be too bad except for the fact that no bad guy/girl impressed me as an interesting character worth rooting for. I also missed the humor of Owen Zastava Pitt. Even enigmatic and emotionless Agent Franks said some great one-liners from time to time. This book was way too serious.<br><br>So my verdict is 3 stars. Would I read the next book? The jury is still out on this one. Oh and by the way if I created an impression that it is a retelling of X-Men, I am sorry. The book is inspired by the comics, but is not a copy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17509676636533875927" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_174888310" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/174888310" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/174888310?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=action">action</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer174888310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6224956776902264177">This is a big greasy double cheeseburger...with all the works kind-of-a book. It's not deep, it's full of action, a rather unique magic system that while you've probably seen things close to...you haven't seen it exactly...adventure, and imagination. I like it. So far I've pretty much liked everything Mr. Correia has turned out.<br/><br/>Maybe if we had a 10 star system here I "might have" given it a 9 as there are a lot of books I'd rate higher. The same goes for a half star system, it might get a 4.5. B</span>
  <span id="freeText6224956776902264177" style="display:none">This is a big greasy double cheeseburger...with all the works kind-of-a book. It's not deep, it's full of action, a rather unique magic system that while you've probably seen things close to...you haven't seen it exactly...adventure, and imagination. I like it. So far I've pretty much liked everything Mr. Correia has turned out.<br /><br />Maybe if we had a 10 star system here I "might have" given it a 9 as there are a lot of books I'd rate higher. The same goes for a half star system, it might get a 4.5. But we don't have either of those, we have an "out of 5 star" rating system, and I think it deserves a bit better than a 4, so...I went to the complete 5. <br /><br />The novel is all story right from the get-go without the slow build up you sometimes get even in action novels. While we don't find out what color socks each person wears or how they feel about polar bears or their favorite snack they are well drawn and complete. You come to know them and care when....well, that would be a spoiler. You'll see influences here from other well done fantasy. Don't get me wrong, the story is very original and shows lots of imaginative thought, it's all Mr. Correia's own, still there are distant echos of so many from H.P. Lovecraft to Sax Rohmer (with maybe a nod to Bob Kane?). <br /><br />The book does something I've seen done before in that Mr. Correia takes actual people from history and re-imagines them into this (very) alternate history where magic has come to exist. As many are people I'm interested in (one way and another) and some I find very interesting (as in for example John Moses Browning or John J. "Black Jack" Pershing). I won't give any details about the way the world's different or the basis for the magic system other than what I've already said. It may slightly resemble things you've seen before, but it's one of the more original systems and alternate histories I've seen.<br /><br />As you may have guessed by now, all in all I like the book. Not great literature but a great read. Maybe not the best, maybe a few gripes, (no need to go into those really. Are you curious? I'll mention one below, but it's no big deal) but nothing to turn me away. I'd say the book is fun, and it is, but there are serious moments and even some emotional moments. Well, done, well told, well written, enjoyed and recommended... enjoy.<br /><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ nothing much here. One reason I might have dropped a half star was that there is a bit, and only a bit of social or political commentary which I agree with mostly, but not entirely. BUT most of that is in imagined quotes in chapter headings and has nothing to do with the story at all. No reason not to read the book if you like Urban Fantasy, Action or both. Very little down side to this bit of brain candy <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />This is a gut-busting, hard fighting, brawny, rugged dose of literary junk food...brain candy at it's best. As said before, enjoy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6224956776902264177" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <td colspan="2">

<div id="review_402007356" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/402007356" />
    <a title="seak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1805180-seak"><img alt="seak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410456529p2/1805180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/402007356?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="seak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="seak" href="/user/show/1805180-seak">seak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=arc-review">arc-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1805180-seak?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer402007356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1370793700468065915">Cool [no, not nearly cool enough]<br/><br/>Cooooool [so now we're not even using our words? Nope]<br/><br/>Super cool [almost makes it less cool ... no]<br/><br/>Very cool [oh, now we're getting so descriptive ... no]<br/><br/>Chilly [apparently the thesaurus isn't working, nope]<br/><br/>Boss [actually on the way to fitting despite going back a few decades, not quite]<br/><br/>Bully [actually getting to the right decade, but still not there]<br/><br/>Cawbullboss aka Coolawesomebullyboss [I was right up above, needed a new word to describe this]<br/><br/>Yep, Hard Magic ree</span>
  <span id="freeText1370793700468065915" style="display:none">Cool [no, not nearly cool enough]<br /><br />Cooooool [so now we're not even using our words? Nope]<br /><br />Super cool [almost makes it less cool ... no]<br /><br />Very cool [oh, now we're getting so descriptive ... no]<br /><br />Chilly [apparently the thesaurus isn't working, nope]<br /><br />Boss [actually on the way to fitting despite going back a few decades, not quite]<br /><br />Bully [actually getting to the right decade, but still not there]<br /><br />Cawbullboss aka Coolawesomebullyboss [I was right up above, needed a new word to describe this]<br /><br />Yep, Hard Magic reeks of cool in the best possible way, especially when read by Bronson Pinchot. Yup, the Perfect Strangers actor is, despite his character, one of the coolest narrators I've ever listened to.<br /><br />Speaking of cool. Jake Sullivan. Jake freaking Sullivan. He's easily the coolest character I've ever read. He's a slow-witted meathead, at least it would appear on the surface, and you would think I would hate him, but that couldn't be farther from the truth. Not only is he actually a very smart guy, but he works hard and keeps his word. And you probably don't want him to keep his word, it usually doesn't bode well for people. <br /><br />This brings me to something I really enjoyed about this book. Correia's magic system in this book is excellent. It's extremely well thought out, but even better is that people can also use it in more ways than it appears. Jake is one of those who has figured out a way to use his magic differently, he's figured out that manipulating things so that he can easily lift them or move them is just a small portion of what his magic can do. It allows him to manipulate gravity much the same as a certain character in The Way of Kings by Brandon Sanderson. <br /><br />I've heard a lot about Larry Correia and never anything less than positive. Already he was on my list of authors to read, but I've obviously taken my sweet time getting there. Let me tell you, I waited far too long.<br /><br />Hard Magic takes place around the time of the Great Depression. It's the early 1930's and things are not going well for people. However, there are oakies, gangsters, pin stripes, and everything cool about this time period. There are also secret organizations, some good and some bad, and there's more to the magic than it first appears. <br /><br />I won't waste your time anymore. This was such a great read, with great characters and a great narrator in Bronson Pinchot, even though it did take some time to warm up to him. His slow drawl for Jake Sullivan was just pure genius. But beware, this may just make you cooler.<br /><br />4.5 out of 5 Stars (very highly recommended)</span>
  <a data-text-id="1370793700468065915" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_741568384" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/741568384" />
    <a title="Tim The Enchanter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5654692-tim-the-enchanter"><img alt="Tim The Enchanter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386188040p2/5654692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/741568384?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tim The Enchanter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tim The Enchanter" href="/user/show/5654692-tim-the-enchanter">Tim The Enchanter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/16032275-hard-magic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654692-tim-the-enchanter?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654692-tim-the-enchanter?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654692-tim-the-enchanter?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer741568384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13373037162320475913"><b> <u> Excellent Magic Noir - 4 Stars </u> </b><br/><br/>Posted to <a href='http://theliterarylawyer.ca/hard-magic-larry-correia-grimnoir-chronicles-1-shelf/' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Literary Lawyer.ca </a><br/><br/>Being that I am a big fan of the gun toting, monster slaying cowboys in Larry Corriea's <i> Monster Hunter International </i> it seemed natural that I would give his other series a shot. I am glad that I did. Correia bends the Urban Fantasy Genre once again by melding elements of noir with alternate history sci fi. The result is a unique reading experience that sets it apart from the Dresden clones.<br/><br/><br/><u> Plot summary </u><br/><br/>For a large portion of </span>
  <span id="freeText13373037162320475913" style="display:none"><b> <u> Excellent Magic Noir - 4 Stars </u> </b><br /><br />Posted to <a href="http://theliterarylawyer.ca/hard-magic-larry-correia-grimnoir-chronicles-1-shelf/" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Literary Lawyer.ca </a><br /><br />Being that I am a big fan of the gun toting, monster slaying cowboys in Larry Corriea's <i> Monster Hunter International </i> it seemed natural that I would give his other series a shot. I am glad that I did. Correia bends the Urban Fantasy Genre once again by melding elements of noir with alternate history sci fi. The result is a unique reading experience that sets it apart from the Dresden clones.<br /><br /><br /><u> Plot summary </u><br /><br />For a large portion of the book, two major parallel storylines are taking place with a few smaller ones for good measure. The first focuses on Jake Sullivan, an ex military, ex con "spiker" (a person able to alter or spike gravity) under the thumb of the government. The second story line focuses on Faye, an Oakie (Gypsy) girl sold to a kind hearted farmer who shared her power as a "Traveler" (a person able to transport themselves from one place to another). After each of the them suffer a series of unfortunate events they each come into contact with a secret society of Actives (people with magical powers). Of course, once they do, all hell breaks loose.<br /><br /><u> The Good </u><br /><br /><b> Great Feel </b><br /><br />The story was atmospheric and the reader has the sense that some of these characters would fit in with a bunch of gangsters in a mob flick or would be solving crimes from their poorly light, smoke filled offices. This is unlike most books in the UF genre which tend to be character centric while the setting is blurred or generic. <br /><br />The novel is deeply rooted in a period of time. While I don`t recall that a date was given, you have the sense that it occurring in the 40`s or 50`s. The difference is that it is not the 40`s and 50`s that show up in our text books. Hitler, Einstein, Tesla, J. Edgar Hoover and a wide array of historical figures existed but their lives and deaths did not necessarily unfold as we remember. Some of them, Einstein and Tesla for example, were Cogs (Actives whose intellect is augmented by magic). At the beginning of each chapter, the author "quotes" historical figures. The quotes are generally related to real events but make reference to appearance or use of magic. This literary device did an excellent job of helping the reader he was reading an alternate history.<br /><br /> <br /><u> The Bad </u><br /><br /><b> It`s the good kind of slow </b> <br /><br />Fans of Monster Hunter International have come to expect specific pace from of Larry Corriea book. Namely, a plot on full auto with a hurricane at its back. This novel on the other hand moves at more leisurely pace. For the most part, this did not bother me. It did seem that from time to time the plot was dragging or some obstacle was put in the way simply to draw out the story. For some lovers of UF the pace with put them off. While it did detract somewhat from book (and ultimately my rating) don`t let it scare you away. The genre mixing style is entertaining and fun.<br /><br /><b> Final Thoughts </b><br /><br />I enjoyed the world building and a magic system that people did not understand. The exploration of how magic suddenly appeared and where it came from is an interesting aspect of the story. Corriea`s ability to draw in the reader and engage them with his story never fails to impress. While Monster Hunter International remains my go to series for all things Larry Corriea, this is an excellent addition to Corriea lore.<br /><br /><u> Audiobook Notes </u><br /><br />The narration was 5 star. The narrator is genius with voices and accents. He does an especially good job of bringing to life two the odd speech patterns of the two unique characters. <br /><br /><b> <u> Content Advisories </u> </b><br /><br />It is difficult to find commentary on the sex/violence/language content of book if you are interested. I make an effort to give you the information so you can make an informed decision before reading. *Disclaimer* I do not take note or count the occurrences of adult language as I read. I am simply giving approximations.<br /><br />Scale 1 - Lowest 5 - Highest<br /><br /><u> Sex </u> - <b> 2 </b><br /><br />There is some sexual tension between a few characters. Once character is revealed to be a former prostitute. Sex is implied on at least one occasion. Overall, the sexual content is low.<br /><br /><u> Language </u> - <b> 3.5 </b><br /><br />Corriea does not shy away from the use of adult language. That said, there is less than in the Monster Hunter International series. Moderate occurrences of mild obscenities and low occurrences of the f-word.<br /><br /><u> Violence </u> - <b> 4 </b><br /><br />There is plenty of magical and gun related violence. As there is war between factions of those who have magic, there are battles on many fronts. There a several scenes where characters are disemboweled and it is moderate to highly graphic. In most every chapter, at least one person is killed by a wide array of means. It is pervasive and occasionally graphic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13373037162320475913" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_237831591" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Beanbag Love" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2598237-beanbag-love"><img alt="Beanbag Love" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249531311p2/2598237.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/237831591?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beanbag Love" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beanbag Love" href="/user/show/2598237-beanbag-love">Beanbag Love</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer237831591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer401853715661677780">This alt-history magic noir series is a great mind-bender. I love Larry Correia's no-holds-barred action writing. His world building in this is fantastic and the attention to detail is superb. I had been told by other fans of Monster Hunter International that this was even better and I think I might agree. <br/><br/>Jake Sullivan is a gravity manipulating "Heavy", forced to do jobs rounding up other magical "Actives" for J. Edgar Hoover. Faye Vierra is a girl of indeterminate age -- a teenager -- who has </span>
  <span id="freeText401853715661677780" style="display:none">This alt-history magic noir series is a great mind-bender. I love Larry Correia's no-holds-barred action writing. His world building in this is fantastic and the attention to detail is superb. I had been told by other fans of Monster Hunter International that this was even better and I think I might agree. <br /><br />Jake Sullivan is a gravity manipulating "Heavy", forced to do jobs rounding up other magical "Actives" for J. Edgar Hoover. Faye Vierra is a girl of indeterminate age -- a teenager -- who has a rare ability and an over-abundance of Power. Delilah is a Brute, Francis is a Mover, Lance can talk through squirrels, Jane can Heal, and Blackjack Pershing is in trouble. It's intricate, driven, even poignant, and it engages completely. The use of real history and people is done with finesse and incredible cleverness. <br /><br />As always, Correia's action sequences are over-the-top and filled with suspense and gore. There's an element of superhero mythology -- one reference made me laugh out loud at the end -- as well as military suspense, steampunk and epic fantasy. <br /><br />Jake does seem like Owen Pitt (the protag from MHI) in a different setting, but that's okay because I love Owen. And this is third person so we get many points of view and they're all fascinating. And, yes, the story structure is also a lot like MHI but, again, I love MHI's story structure so I have no complaints. The rich detail of this imagined world is so full and unique I can't imagine the similarity of one character is going to bother anyone too much. <br /><br />Check your political correctness at the door! This is noir written in the context and verbiage of 1920's/30's post-war America. And what impresses me so much is the accuracy of tone and general worldview of the time coupled with the outrageous aspects of the fantasy element. Correia has done an amazing job.<br /><br />I had one complaint but it's a spoiler so I won't tell. It wasn't enough to lower the rating, however. <br /><br />Now to distract myself so I don't plow through the next one and end up with nothing left. </span>
  <a data-text-id="401853715661677780" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2055954438" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2055954438" />
    <a title="Skip" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1389748-skip"><img alt="Skip" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1231161516p2/1389748.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2055954438?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Skip" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Skip" href="/user/show/1389748-skip">Skip</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781451638240" href="/book/show/12253598-hard-magic">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1389748-skip?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2055954438" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17560737519503258897">Correia's Hard Magic is a genre-crossing novel: epic, urban fantasy, alternative history, steampunk, noir-detective thriller all rolled into a single story. The story is set in the 1920s and 1930s, with the Japanese seeking supremacy after Germany has been subdued. At the heart are two complex, but well-developed characters in the classic good vs. evil battle. First, Jake Sullivan can alter his personal gravity (a "Heavy.") He has been recently paroled to assist the Feds in capturing criminals, </span>
  <span id="freeText17560737519503258897" style="display:none">Correia's Hard Magic is a genre-crossing novel: epic, urban fantasy, alternative history, steampunk, noir-detective thriller all rolled into a single story. The story is set in the 1920s and 1930s, with the Japanese seeking supremacy after Germany has been subdued. At the heart are two complex, but well-developed characters in the classic good vs. evil battle. First, Jake Sullivan can alter his personal gravity (a "Heavy.") He has been recently paroled to assist the Feds in capturing criminals, and is assigned to capture a former girlfriend. Well read and thoughtful, he and his brothers served his country in war with distinction. Second is Faye, whose rare magical gift is teleportation (a "Traveler.") Faye suffers through traumatic events early in the novel, but grows in strength and character, seeking vengeance for the senseless murder of his adoptive grandfather. The book's magic system and world-building was a bit slow for my taste, and I found one of the storylines superfluous, but enjoyed the novel, and look forward to reading more of the Grimnoir Chronicles.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17560737519503258897" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_824916512" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/824916512" />
    <a title="David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3335664-david"><img alt="David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551667298p2/3335664.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/824916512?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David" href="/user/show/3335664-david">David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/16032275-hard-magic">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Okie teleporters, red-headed magical ninja, New Orleans madames with super-strength</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=superheroes">superheroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=great-villains">great-villains</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=american-fantasy">american-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=alternate-history">alternate-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=cheesy-dumb-fun">cheesy-dumb-fun</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335664-david?shelf=1930s">1930s</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer824916512" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2544993451134337220">Contrary to its title, <i>Hard Magic</i> is not an urban fantasy: it's basically a superhero novel. Set in an alternate history between world wars, a mysterious alien "power" came to Earth in the middle of the 19th century and granted a subset of the population magical powers. For the majority of "Actives," these powers come in singular and well-defined forms: there are "brutes" who have super strength, "torches" who are pyrokinetics, "mouths" with mind control powers, "heavies" who can manipulate grav</span>
  <span id="freeText2544993451134337220" style="display:none">Contrary to its title, <i>Hard Magic</i> is not an urban fantasy: it's basically a superhero novel. Set in an alternate history between world wars, a mysterious alien "power" came to Earth in the middle of the 19th century and granted a subset of the population magical powers. For the majority of "Actives," these powers come in singular and well-defined forms: there are "brutes" who have super strength, "torches" who are pyrokinetics, "mouths" with mind control powers, "heavies" who can manipulate gravity, etc. But it turns out there are also other forms of magic, such as those wielded by the Japanese Imperium's "Iron Guard." These magical super-soldiers have kanji branded into their skins that give them accelerated healing, protection from harm, strength and speed, and other powers. There are also necromancers who raise the dead to create zombie armies, and other manifestations of magical power, but they all function pretty much like super powers.<br /><br />In this alternate history, Japan is on a path to world domination thanks to possessing the most powerful and heavily trained magical warriors, and fleets of dirigibles that function like bombers and aircraft carriers all at once. Led by the most powerful man on Earth (literally and figuratively), Chairman Tokugawa, this is the Japan of the 1930s: expansionist, fascist, and unambiguously and unapologetically the bad guys. Tokugawa, as the Big Bad, is a great if somewhat stereotyped villain. Yes, he's a centuries-old samurai with magical superpowers who goes on about strength and honor and likes to recite poems to his enemies before killing them, but he has class and style and he's the sort of villain you love to see chewing the scenery and can't wait for the climactic battle where he finally goes down.<br /><br />This book has <em>lots</em> of climactic battles, each one more epic than the last. Jake Sullivan, the main character, is a "heavy" who can control gravity. He's also a great big slab of macho, a war veteran, an ex-con, an ex-P.I., fearless alpha, and probably a little bit of an authorial wish-fulfillment. He hits every manly-man trope in the noir genre, and you know what? <em>That's okay!</em> Because this book is what it is, a raging male power fantasy like the classic superhero comics where Superman knocked Nazi fighter planes out of the sky. Here we have Jake Sullivan fighting other "Actives," then pitted against his own brother, who of course is bigger and badder than him and thus is the penultimate Boss level Jake must get past before he can face the Chairman himself.<br /><br />But it's not just Jake tromping around in a California fortified with "Peace Rays" created by Tesla and fighting Imperium ninjas and invincible Iron Guards and dirigible sky pirates. He joins the Knights of the Grimnoir, an international organization dedicated to protecting the magically gifted and the non-magical alike. Jake's ex is Delilah, a former New Orleans whore with super-strength. A secondary protagonist is Faye, an Okie "Traveler" (teleporter) who is a hoot as a character, her mind running a mile a minute in a hundred directions, and in the climax (in which she, like Jake, has without a whole lot of plausible explanation powered up by a factor of about eleventy) is running amok through the Japanese dirigible fleet blasting magical ninjas with a shotgun that never seems to run out of ammo, and that's before she and Jake go completely Super Saiyan against the Chairman and his Iron Guard.<br /><br />If you're thinking this sounds a lot like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/583808563" rel="nofollow noopener">Steelheart</a> or <i>Mistborn</i>, you're right. This was my first Larry Correia novel, but his writing style and his worldbuilding reminded me a lot of Brandon Sanderson. Like Sanderson, Correia writes straight-up action/adventure with lots of heroics and over-the-top power stunts and characters who are often archetypes more than fully-realized people, but if you are in the mood for grand pulp adventure, this book hits a high mark and <em>almost</em> got 5 stars from me. It is a guns blazing, powers activating, bloody spectacular pulp superhero slugfest that is, if not a literary masterpiece and unabashedly un-PC, absolutely great fun for those who like an occasional dose of fist-pumping "America, booyah!" heroics.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2544993451134337220" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_review_824916512'><a id="like_count_review_824916512" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/824916512?resource_type=Review"><span class="likesCount">8 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F8643407-hard-magic">Like</a></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_197574719" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/197574719" />
    <a title="Kat  Hooper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2177891-kat-hooper"><img alt="Kat  Hooper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533675060p2/2177891.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/197574719?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat  Hooper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat  Hooper" href="/user/show/2177891-kat-hooper">Kat  Hooper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2177891-kat-hooper?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer197574719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15592882497569635134">ORIGINALLY POSTED AT <a href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Literature</a>.<br/><br/>Jake Sullivan is not your average Heavy. He spent his jail time honing his skills and improving his mind and now he’s J. Edgar Hoover’s super-weapon, useful for fighting Fades, Torches, Brutes, and any of the other Actives who are using their magic for criminal purposes. Jake doesn’t like being used this way, but it’s his ticket out of prison. When the FBI asks Jake to bring down Delilah Jones, the Brute who used to be his girlfriend, Jake gets caught up i</span>
  <span id="freeText15592882497569635134" style="display:none">ORIGINALLY POSTED AT <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Literature</a>.<br /><br />Jake Sullivan is not your average Heavy. He spent his jail time honing his skills and improving his mind and now he’s J. Edgar Hoover’s super-weapon, useful for fighting Fades, Torches, Brutes, and any of the other Actives who are using their magic for criminal purposes. Jake doesn’t like being used this way, but it’s his ticket out of prison. When the FBI asks Jake to bring down Delilah Jones, the Brute who used to be his girlfriend, Jake gets caught up in a world-wide battle that involves magic, mobsters, zombies, zeppelins, Ninjas and Nikola Tesla’s peace ray.<br /><br />Knowing that Larry Correia was into big guns and B movies, I wasn’t planning to pick up Hard Magic, the first of his Grimnoir Chronicles. It doesn’t really sound like my kind of thing. But then I noticed that it was released in audio by Audible Frontiers (who always do a superb production) and narrated by actor Bronson Pinchot. I decided to give it a shot, and I’m glad I did. Even though it is a bit too gory for me, Hard Magic is an exciting story with a fully-developed world, a cool magic system, terrific characters, and some hard-hitting action scenes.<br /><br />I won’t even try to classify Hard Magic — it’s urban, it’s alternate history, it’s paranormal, it’s steampunk, it’s romance, it’s horror, it’s noir — it’s a little bit of everything. The story is set in an alternate 20th century between WWI and WWII. Magic talents have evolved in some humans so that each Active has one particular skill. For example, Jake Sullivan can alter gravitational forces, making himself or other objects light or heavy, Torches can set or put out fires, and Brutes have super strength. In addition to these heritable magical skills, the Germans have developed a way to create zombies to keep their soldiers fighting during The Great War, and the Japanese have developed their own nearly indestructible human super-weapons which they call the Iron Guard. And everyone wants to find the missing pieces of the machine that Nikola Tesla was working on at Wardenclyffe.<br /><br />There’s a lot going on in the Grimnoir Chronicles, but Correia gives us a break by setting it in our own almost-recognizable world. The bits of true history orient the reader, and the mangled quotes of real historical figures at the beginning of each chapter give Hard Magic an authentic feel:<br /><br /> * I am by heritage a Jew, by citizenship a Swiss, by magical gift a Cog, and by makeup a human being, and only a human being, without any special attachment to any state or national entity whatsoever. —Albert Einstein, 1919<br /> * You can go a long way with a smile. You can go a lot farther with a smile and a gun. A smile, a gun, and a Brute get you the key to the city. —Al “Scarface” Capone, 1930<br /><br />Hard Magic is well-written and frequently funny. The complex and twisty plot moves swiftly and is full of intriguing characters such as the uneducated orphan who can Travel, the German Fade who walks through walls, the Pale Horse whose curse kills, the greedy billionaire who designs airships... there are too many interesting characters to list. All of their cool magical skills lead to some hardcore fight scenes. Most readers will probably find these fights to be the most fun part of the book. I was grossed out more than once and kind of irked that dead people didn’t necessarily stay dead, but that’s just me.<br /><br />If you’re familiar with Bronson Pinchot’s acting career, it won’t surprise you to learn that his narration of the audiobook was brilliant. He took the whole production to a higher level. He easily managed all those characters with their different ethnicities and education levels — it was delightful, and was one of the best audiobook performances I’ve ever heard.<br /><br />Despite my queasiness, I’m looking forward to Spellbound, the next novel in the Grimnoir Chronicles. I can highly recommend this series to urban fantasy/noir fans who don’t mind reading about ripped off heads and steaming entrails. If you want to give it a try, read the first few chapters of Hard Magic at Larry Correia’s blog.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15592882497569635134" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_548296150" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/548296150" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/548296150?book_show_action=true">Feb 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=dystopias">dystopias</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=the_south">the_south</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=zombies">zombies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=humorous">humorous</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=politicalish">politicalish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer548296150" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4269246691585165182">4.5 Stars <br/><br/>I downloaded this book from Audible way back in February, but I hadn't touched it since then. It could be that I tried to start Correia's Monster Hunter International series a couple times, but it just didn't grab me, and so I thought this one would be the same way. I was very wrong about that. <br/><br/>Almost from the first line I was drawn into this story. I loved it, and have every intention of finishing out the series and getting back to the MHI series. <br/><br/>I do think that quite a large part of</span>
  <span id="freeText4269246691585165182" style="display:none">4.5 Stars <br /><br />I downloaded this book from Audible way back in February, but I hadn't touched it since then. It could be that I tried to start Correia's Monster Hunter International series a couple times, but it just didn't grab me, and so I thought this one would be the same way. I was very wrong about that. <br /><br />Almost from the first line I was drawn into this story. I loved it, and have every intention of finishing out the series and getting back to the MHI series. <br /><br />I do think that quite a large part of my enjoyment of this book was due to Bronson Pinchot's reading though. I followed along in the e-book for a good chunk of this because I wanted to see some of the terms that I was hearing, and I realized that he wasn't just reading the book aloud, he was <i>performing</i> it. He wheezed, he croaked, he mumbled, he did the accents... and I liked it. His cadence and accent while reading The Pale Horse brought that character to life so much more than the words on the page alone would have. I know that this is a complete turnaround from my long-held stance against readers "doing the voices", but in this case, I feel like it benefited the book more than it got in the way of it. (But, on the other hand, the ebook edition did have lovely sketches of some of the characters, and I really enjoyed those!)<br /><br />I will say that there were times when I wished he'd have gone in a different direction with the reading, though. For instance, I LOVED the way that he voiced Jake Sullivan, and I found myself wishing that he had more dialogue so I could listen to more of him. But Jake is a very large man, even among big men, so when he yells, I expect a bellowing roar. What I got was more of a slightly raised voice. It was OK, but I wished he'd just go for it and make me really FEEL the intensity and urgency of the moment that made quiet Jake need to yell in the first place. <br /><br />Or, another example, sometimes he'd end a sentence with a slightly higher tone than I thought it should have had. To me, the sentence "He was pissed." is one that should almost be read staccato, and the last word should be either the same tone and inflection as the other two, or slightly lower. To me, it sounds SERIOUS that way. Dangerous. You don't want to fuck with him when he's pissed. But Pinchot would sometimes read sentences like that with a slightly raised inflection at the end. Not quite enough to make it sound questioning, but more as if it was amusing, and it just seemed strange to me. <br /><br />But other than these little things, I thought that he did a fantastic job reading the book, and I hope that he reads the entire series because now that his performance is in my head, I don't think that anyone else would be able to hold a candle to it. Not even myself, in the unlikely event that I were to continue in text form. <br /><br />But enough about the audio itself. This story was fascinating, and I really enjoyed it. I loved the characters, and I loved the magic system, and I loved the conflicts and the tone and the setting and... well pretty much everything. <br /><br />I loved the alternate history style. I haven't read very many alt-hist books, but the ones that I have, I enjoyed quite a bit. I think that I will need to read more of these, because I'm not sure if it's the novelty of seeing real historical figures and events morphed into very different versions that I enjoyed, or the skill of Correia's execution in doing so. But honestly, it doesn't matter, because I DID like it, and that's enough for me. <br /><br />I definitely want to learn more about the umm... source of the magic, and more about the different skills that the Grimnoir mentioned but that we didn't much get to see in action. I want to live in this world for a while, so I'll definitely be picking up the other books in the series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4269246691585165182" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_333399658" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/333399658" />
    <a title="Ryan Draga" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4855020-ryan-draga"><img alt="Ryan Draga" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519400927p2/4855020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/333399658?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ryan Draga" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ryan Draga" href="/user/show/4855020-ryan-draga">Ryan Draga</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer333399658" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11558391053329457126">I've now read this along with Book 2 of the series (entitled "Spellbound"). I found this on a whim as an audiobook on Audible whilst looking for something for my girlfriend. I had a few free monthly credits thanks to a promotion, so I snagged both books.<br/><br/>First off, for novelty's sake I should note that the audiobooks are (quite wonderfully) narrated by none other than Bronson Pinchot...known to most of us 80s kids as Balki from Perfect Strangers.<br/><br/>Now I'll be honest here, when I saw a pulpy-looking</span>
  <span id="freeText11558391053329457126" style="display:none">I've now read this along with Book 2 of the series (entitled "Spellbound"). I found this on a whim as an audiobook on Audible whilst looking for something for my girlfriend. I had a few free monthly credits thanks to a promotion, so I snagged both books.<br /><br />First off, for novelty's sake I should note that the audiobooks are (quite wonderfully) narrated by none other than Bronson Pinchot...known to most of us 80s kids as Balki from Perfect Strangers.<br /><br />Now I'll be honest here, when I saw a pulpy-looking, steampunk-bandwagon-riding alt. history/hard-boiled noir book narrated by an 80's castaway known for an over-the-top comedic character, I snapped the book up expecting a trainwreck involving everything I just described. However...a trainwreck, it was CERTAINLY not.<br /><br />On the COMPLETE contrary, this book (and it's sequel) was FANTASTIC. I couldn't stop listening. I got these as an excuse to have a chuckle whilst doing housework, and instead found myself putting down the mop and broom and becoming completely lost in this wonderfully-imagined alternate version of the world where Magic existed alongside early 20th century technology and culture...the book has small tidbits of information (which it often opens chapters with) regarding historical and cultural icons who happened to also have been "actives" (what the book calls magic users who have a proper grasp on their abilities). <br /><br />Beyond that singular curiosity though, there is certainly much more. The characters are wonderful and a motley bunch to be certain: a hard-boiled ex-con turned FBI muscle that can manipulate gravity, a femme fatale with physicality that would make the Hulk crap his giant purple shorts, a firecracker hayseed girl who can teleport, a famous big game hunter who makes Doctor Doolittle look like a chump...the list goes on. There's A LOT of story packed into this book.<br /><br />TL;DR version: if you're a sucker for steampunk and/or alt. history, if you're a Dresden Files fan, hell, beyond all that, if you love a good old fashioned "good guys versus bad guys" pulp yarn, PICK THIS DAMN BOOK UP. I guarantee you won't put it down.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11558391053329457126" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
